<Author>pinkpeche
<Content>Great Location I used points to stay here and was only charged a minimal upgrade fee per night. The rooms are on the small side like every other place in Europe... but we were upgraded to a decent size room in order to fit a rollaway bed (for my boyfriend's daughter). The hotel staff is quite friendly and English skills were impressive. Paris has come a long way accomodating English speaking patrons. I'm not sure if this is for everyone, but we received complimentary breakfast every morning in the dining area which ends at 10:30 am. The food was plentiful with a lot of options. The hotel is conveniently located near the Louvre and Musee d'Orsay and near three different subway stops. I find Paris's subway system very easy to navigate... so definitely take advantage of the subway system.

<Content>Lovely staff, great location, weird picture in lift My husband and I stayed here for one night to see the Rodrigo and Gabriela concert at Bataclan. He is a regular Marriott traveller and raves about their beds, sheets and service - and he is right. You could have fitted an entire country into the bed - and it was marvelous. Oh and allowing smokers in the rooms - the smell permeates.........But for me it is the location and the staff that make a place - not the little itty bitty irritations that people can dwell on and it was fab. Concert was brill too!

<Content>Nice Size, Great Staff, A plus I have nothing but good things to state about this hotel, my wife and I stayed 4 nights in early Sept. We booked a Prestige Room, which was large by Paris standards, the price at the time was around 350 Euros, did not do any packages. Overall the room was well appointed, had a modern feel, but not over the top. There were large French Doors that opened to overlook a courtyard that was actually the glass ceiling of the reception area, different, but made the room more open.One thing I liked about this hotel was the size related to amenities. It is a relatively small hotel, but had everything you may want onsite, Restaurant, Room Service, Lobby Bar, Concierge, and a great Pool and Gym.We used the Concierge extensively before we arrived and during the stay, I cannot say enough about them, all we spoke to were knowledgeable and helpful. In general, all the staff was very nice.Regarding location, the hotel is very close to the Louve, Tuileries, Place Vendome and Musee D'Orsay. All within a short walk. So if this is a first trip to Paris, I cannot think of a much better location.All in all, a great place, I would stay again.

<Author>margo1116
<Content>Great Location--Beware Small Rooms My husband and I recently spent four days in Paris and chose to stay on the Right Bank. We loved the location of the Renaissance Vendome -- an easy walk to the Left Bank and lots of great restaurants and museums within walking distance or easy Metro ride. We originally opted for the most economical room but realized after one night that the cramped quarters just didn't work for us. We found another hotel nearby that was less expensive and had larger rooms. We called management to advise them of our upcoming departure and explained the reason for our departure. We were immediately upgraded to the next size room which worked perfectly for us. We've learned to speak up and be polite complainers. Breakfasts were included in our American Express package. They were certainly adequate, but definitely not worth the price in Euros. Lots of nearby cafes and restaurants would have worked just as well. The staff was accommodating and pleasant and we would not hesitate to stay there again; it didn't have a real Parisian feel to it --very contemporary rooms, etc. but everything worked -- great shower and modern bathtub, nice plasma TV and Bulgari amenities. Our Amex package also included free wireless. Enjoy!

<Author>SeasonedTrvlr
<Content>Almost all Americans and touristy location, but nice rooms and pool. 1) About 80% of the people there at least were Americans, most in their 50's. In my opinion that's an ambiance-reducer when you're in Paris, but may not be a big deal to you.2) Breakfast is 29Euros per person, find a rate with breakfast included or be prepared to walk somewhere else. Free wifi in the lobby.3) Nice relaxing pool, not a lap pool, but good for big kids. Nice lounges next to the pool.4) Workout room is pretty small but has a good amount of TVs.5) Location is near pricey boutiques and the touristy Rue de Rivoli. Also nicely close to the Louvre (5 min walk) and the Tuilleries which I love. So a push in this regard in my opinion.6) Room was small but nice, great comfortable bed, fantastic bathroom with separate shower and tub (I had a Superior room, 1 level above the base Deluxe room). Frankly I can't imagine how small a Deluxe room would be so I'd at least spring for the Superior.7) Room had a DVD player, so bring your movies if you like (no PPV). About 6 English TV stations including CNBC, CNN, BBC12, Eurosport, and France 24 of course.8) Lobby has a very nice, intimate wood-buring fireplace.9) Takes them about 10-15 minutes to get you a taxi.If you like seafood I went to Gaya in the Left Bank (across the street from L'Atelier Joel Rubechon for those who know). Fantastic seafood, but not cheap. If you're a sea-foodie then you should try it.

<Author>Viaggiamo
<Content>Comfortable, Great location for Family of 5 We recently stayed at this hotel w/our 3 sons ages 14, 11  7. We had connecting rooms which was very convenient. The rooms large, as many people have commented on this site, but I didn't find them to be much smaller than any other big city hotel, esp. for Europe, similar to what you might expect in NYC.The rooms were nicely done. The beds were excellent, which is always so easy to find in France. The bathrooms are good. The hotel itself is a very nice renovated building - nice French doors  windows. It is however beginning to show the first signs of some wear - mainly the carpet  the bathrooms did have some mildew that should probably be taken care of.It is a courtyard building with the lobby in the center under a skylight. My kids enjoyed using the pool - which really is more of an adult spa kind of setting. The location could not be beat. It's on a quiet side street located very close to the Place Vendome. It is a couple minute walk to the Jardin Tuliere  maybe 5 minutes or so to the Louvre. You can also walk to the shopping area around the department store Printemps. We walked to the Eiffel Tower - about a 20-30 minute walk - but pleasant. You can easily walk to the Batobus (water taxi) stop at Musee d'Orsay  get around that way up  down the Seine.The hotel staff all speaks excellent English. The concierge recommended a brasserie called Cafe Flottes (sp?) which is about a 5 min walk or so. We ate lunch there twice  dinner once. The food is very good  w/in reason. We were able to book our rooms using Marriott points. Not sure what prices are like for similar hotels in the same location.

<Content>Great Oasis in the big city My son and I stayed here July 13 for 5 nights. I loved the hotel. It is contemporary, hip and comfortable. I found the hotel to be a nice oasis from the bustle of Paris. The room was a bit small, but we didn't need anymore room for just the two of us. We hardly were in the room. The hotel staff, I found to be very friendly and accommodating. The internet is expensive, but c'est la vie in France. There is an internet cafe not too far from the hotel if you really need to use the internet for a period of time.Great location to fantastic shopping and restaurants galore, not to mention just a stones throw from the Louvre and Tuilleries. Plus, two of my favorite chocolatiers are right around the corner. Jean Paul Haven and Michel Cuizel. In fact, at turn down the hotel puts a chocolate sucker on your pillow. We didn't get it every night and most nights they only left one, but WOW the chocoate is to die for. I knew I should have asked for more!Would stay here again and I do recommend the hotel.

<Author>ColonialKay
<Content>The Renaissance Paris Vendome put the "happy" in our birthdays! We recently returned from a three-night stay at the Renaissance Vendome, and we hope to return some day. After we completed business elsewhere in Europe, we went to Paris to make our 60th birthdays more palatable! The ambiance is serenely upscale, the employees are extremely helpful and polite, and the location cannot be beat. It is pricey, but luckily, we used Marriott points for free nights and spent less than $300 to upgrade to a king-size room which included breakfast. There were a couple, minor negatives. The bed was a little large for the width of the room, so we had to be careful not to stub our toes going into the bathroom. Also, we had to learn to shut the shower door without pinching our fingers. Saying that, the huge vases of orchids, the bowls of candy and fruit, and the pitchers of citrus-infused water in the lobby were welcoming sights. Our room was very comfortable and stylish with luxury fabrics, a flat screen TV, and a back-friendly mattress. A box of luscious chocolate-covered nuts, a free bottle of good water, and a vase with real flowers greeted us when we checked into the room; chocolate lollipops nestled on our pillows at night. The bathroom was large with a warming rack, a shower, and a tub, plus there was ample closet and storage space. The view was of a small, interior courtyard, which was just fine, because the room was very quiet. We did not have to contend with traffic noise.The restaurant was very good; in fact, Frommer recommends La Pinxo in his guidebook. It is the moderate-priced restaurant of a two-star Michlelin-rated chef. We celebrated our birthdays there one night, enjoying a bottle of champagne and entrees of tuna and lamb, both excellent. Breakfast was a buffet with a hot dish station, a cereal station, a cheese, salmon, and meats station, and a bread and pastry station. We did order poached eggs one day and surprisingly found them to be tough, but we didn't mind because we had so many other good choices to eat instead. The next day, we noticed another couple commenting on the tough poached eggs! The scrambled eggs, part of the hot dish station, were excellent in comparison.The wait staff, the front desk help, and the concierges were all top rate, so friendly and helpful. At the hotel, we were able to buy museum passes and our tickets for a night time Seine tour--both time savers. The hotel also recommended Au Pied De Cochan, which filled my desire to eat at an old, traditional French restaurant. It has been around since 1946 and touts that it is the creator of the original recipe for French onion soup. The soup was yummy--the best French onion soup we ever ate! As I stated above, the location is convenient to most of Paris's major attractions. We walked almost everywhere we went, so we could soak up the city's ambience. We saved a lot of money by not having to take taxis and trains in most cases.Even though there were a couple things that were not perfect, I am still giving the hotel a perfect rating. I have never been in a hotel yet that didn't have at least a couple minor glitches. Overall, this was a great hotel which did, indeed, help make our birthdays happy ones!

<Author>mattrLondon
<Content>Nice small hotel We stayed at this hotel for one night in late June 2008. We stayed in a deluxe room which was pretty typical for Paris - really expensive (450 euros per night) and less than half the size of a similar priced room in any other city in the world. But this is to be expected in Paris. The room (notwithstanding the size) was nice - well appointed and clean, although I was a little disappointed as we had requested a non-smoking room and it definitely smelled of smoke. Our room had a small balcony overlooking the street which was very pretty. The staff were friendly and helpful. Breakfast in the hotel was very good. The hotel is very centrally located, 2 minutes from the Lourve and within an easy walk of most of the things that people like to do when in Paris. By way of comparison I have stayed at the Hilton Arc de Triomphe before (about the same price) and this hotel is better if you are a tourist while the Hilton is better if you are travelling for business. Overall I thought that this was a good hotel and I would go back or recommend it.

<Author>BiscottiCalifornia
<Content>Good Business Hotel... Average for Vacationers After much research I booked this hotel for a multi-night stay several weeks ago. It's a beautiful hotel in many respects but as with most Paris hotels the rooms are small and the prices are stratospheric... in our case even in an upgraded prestige room we felt a little claustrophobic at over $600 US a night.What's great... recently renovated, fast internet access, clean rooms, comfortable bed, stylish interiors, nice bathrooms... had both tub and shower in our prestige room, great english speaking staff, and location (in some respects... more on that in the next section.)What's not so great... hotel ambiance is a bit on the quiet side which is great if you're traveling on business and are just looking for a place to crash but not a good if you're looking to have a drink in the lobby bar and soak up the atmosphere of Paris. The rooms are small... very small. The prices in June were pretty crazy for what you received. The location IS within walking distance of the Louvre, the D'Orsay (a bit longer) and the subway, but the biggest downside of all is that hotel itself is on a bit of a back street with service entrances for other hotels facing Tuileries Gardens and Rue de Rivoli generally occupying one side of the street. For the price I pictured walking out of the hotel onto a tree lined street with cafes, just know that's not what you'll find. Last thing is that we found the area to be devoid of good restaurants (could have missed them obviously)... it's pretty much tourist fare in sidewalk cafes.For the price, ambiance (pretty generic to any hotel in the world) and location I would not stay here again on a pleasure trip... it just doesn't feel enough like Paris. On business I would think about it.

<Author>DennyBoy
<Content>Almost a 5 Star This is a really nice hotel in a great location. The room was small and modern, but incredibly well designed and very attractive. The bathroom had what was by far the best shower I have ever encountered in a Paris hotel in over 30 visits. The staff was universally welcoming and competent. There are many nice touches like bowls of candy at reception and pitchers of cold water in the lobby. They are clearly trying hard to do a good job. I would rate it 5 star except for two things which are becoming pet peeves of mine: exorbitant wifi charges and exorbitant minibar prices. A 500 ml bottle of Fiji water will set you back $12.63 plus tax. This is about 14 times the RETAIL price in the US which is simply a rip-off. You should not have to pay so much or perhaps anything for a decent glass of water in your room. The same goes for wifi at about $24.00 a day which is close to my MONTHLY bill at home in the US. It should be part of the room cost. it is a utility like running water and electricity. Fortunately, Many hotels are starting to provide wifi and drinking water at no extra charge. Curiously, this policy is still far more common at the low end than in luxury hotels which seem to nickel and dime you far more. I hope that the Renaissance Paris Vendome sees the light and joins this trend. When it does, it will be a five star hotel in my book.

<Author>pignacious
<Content>Renaissance Vendome - fantastic hotel We stayed 6 nights at this hotel  it was fantastic. The first 2 nights we stayed in the deluxe room. This is a very small room so be prepared for it. We had 2 medium sized  one small piece of luggage. There was hardly any room to store them. We also were on the 2nd floor and found it fairly noisy late at night for about an hour or so because of the bar across the street. I guess they drag out the garbage bins  stuff at closing.We were able to switch rooms for the next 4 nights, still on the 2nd floor but room overlooked the courtyard of hotel. Very quiet. This room was a Prestige room  it was spectacular. Very large, bathroom has separate WC, tub  shower with ample storage space. Loved this room. Both rooms had very comfortable beds.Breakfast was included with our stay and it was really nice but I would not pay the 29 Euros or so that they charge for it.The location is fantastic. Only a couple of minutes walk to subway stop. Subway is very easy to use  2 euro for each ride or less if you buy a carnat of 10 tickets. There are a number of reasonably priced restaurants on Place du Marche Saint-Honore which is only a couple of short blocks from the hotel. There is also a laundromat on this street. We even did laundry while we ate one night at one of the sidewalk cafes.The staff are very professional, friendly  extremely helpful. One of the best trained staff we have experienced in our travels. They really try to make your stay the best it can be and then some. The concierge will purchase the museum pass as well as other things (Laduree macaroons being one) before your stay for a minimal charge.The Renaissance Vendome is a very good hotel in a great location. We would not hesitate to stay here again.

<Content>An absolute gem in a fantastic location! We spent 6 memorable days in Paris and stayed at this hotel during our visit. First of all, the location is perfect. It centrally located to all the major attractions, and getting around was easy. It was small in size but I say most would consider it large for a typical city room. They had lots of fresh fruit, cheese, deli meat, yogurt, scrambled eggs, bacon, sausage, breads and pastries. The regular rate for the breakfast buffet alone was 30 euro.In addition to the location, what really made this hotel stand out was the service. We talked to 3 different concierges during the course of our stay, and every one of them was very helpful and gave us some excellent advice. I step out on a limb and say it was the best concierge service wee ever had and wee stayed at a lot of hotels over the years.We stay here again in a heartbeat and we can wait to visit Paris again!

<Author>Jakesmum
<Content>Great hotel, loved it! We chose this hotel based on reviews on this site and we were not disappointed, this is a great hotel. The hotel is on Rue du Mont Thabor a little side street parallel (one down) with Rue Saint Honore which has some lovely designer shops and also useful shops like a chemist, an off licence ,etc. If you are looking for jewellery go to Place Vendome, off Rue Saint Honore. As others have said the location is excellent, about 5 minutes walk from the Louvre. After much consideration we decided to take a taxi from the airport rather than brave public transport with large suitcases. It was definitely the stress free way to travel, although obviously more expensive at around 40 - 50 euros for the trip.We were given a lovely room on the 5th floor facing the front of the hotel with a small balcony. It was heaven sitting out on the balcony sipping french wine in the sunshine after a long day walking round Paris. We had superb weather the entire time which helped!The room was not particularly large and neither was the bathroom but both were clean, well laid out and well decorated and had everything you needed, eg safe, mini bar, desk and chair, internet connection, easy chair, etc. Comfy big bed with comfy pillows. My only issue would be with the shower which was a mixer taps over the bath type one. The temperature and water pressure were variable, presumably depending on who else was using their shower at the same time! The air con was great so at night the room was cool, dark and also quiet - perfect!Dont eat breakfast in the hotel unless its part of your package. If its not it costs 58 euros for two and although its a good spread its just not worth that much. Go to Rue Rivoli where there are loads of cafes (out of the hotel, turn left then first right and its the first street you come to, with the Jardin des Tuileries opposite). We liked The Carrousel which is on Rue Rivoli almost opposite Les Arts Decoratif. We didnt eat dinner in the hotel so cant comment on that. We went to the restaurant Les Flottes the first night (the concierges are really helpful re restaurants) and had a great steak. Not cheap but then this is Paris! In fact our only real gripe about the whole holiday would be the price of food and drink - I didnt think it could be that bad compared to Edinburgh or London, but I was wrong! Although we speak some french, all the staff we met spoke excellent english and were really helpful.All in all we had a fantastic time in this hotel and will definitely be going back.I will be detailing hints and tips on the Paris Forum so if you are going soon, check it out.

<Author>Local-Beer
<Content>Paris - A place to be in the center of things This was a very interesting hotel, as it resides on a small side street just around the corner from The Hotel Ritz and the Tulleries. The front desk personnel were fabulous, knowledgable of the area and exstemely professional. From here a must to visit - a short walk to The New York Harry's Bar whare for bourbon drinkers, they have Knob Creek Bourbon and good hot dogs. For a higher time there is the Hemingway Bar at the Ritz, be sure to get Collin the make you a special drink and empress the ladies. He is one of the top ten mixologists and his mixes will astound you. Besides that you will meet both tourists and locals. They will make your evening interesting at the least. At the holel ask about the little bistros down the street for breakfast and dinner, they are more that happy to introduce you to the neighborhood. That what makes this special along with the Irish Pud just across the street - food and drink is great. The turn down service was perfect, the room had a great bath with lots of HOT water, plenty of towels, a robe and slippers. The best of all worlds was that this property actually takes care of anything you might leave in the room at checkout. I happened to leave my drivers license in the safe when I left. When I arrived in Brussels I realised this and had my hotel call for me. The hotel had the item and forwarded it to me at my next stop in Amsterdam, it was there when I arrived. WHAT A RELIEF!!!!!!!! That makes this my number ONE hotel in Paris from now on, as well as there being this Iris Pub across the street run by Chicagoians. Stay and enjoy.

<Author>NCdoc1
<Content>Intimate, elegant Have been to Paris twice before, this was the best hotel / best visit...Location initially slightly daunting, a small one-way street one block north of the Jardins du Tuileries, looked deserted the first day, felt cozy by the end of the week . Between rue de Rivoli and Rue St. Honore, 2 blocks from the Metro, about 4 from the Louvre and Place Concorde. Many fine shops, cafes, brasseries nearby.ALL staff (desk, housekeeping, bellmen) friendly, efficient, accomodating, with most needs anticipated, any others addressed as soon as possible. Concierges knowledgeable and very helpful.Room typically small, as is usual in Paris, but with tall windows, so plenty of natural light, as well as much better average room lighting, in number, location, and brightness of lighting (including moveable halogen lights mounted on the headboard for reading).Restaurant prices high, but so many nearby choices, not a problem.Highly recommend, will stay here again!!

<Content>Loved it! My husband and I stayed at this hotel in November 2007. We decided to stay here because we could stay using Marriott Reward points. Our reservation was for a Prestige Room and we were going to pay an extra 60 Euros a night for our seven day stay.Check in was a little slow. We talked about cancelling our trip due to the transportation strike, but decided to go because we had such a great location. The strike lasted our entire visit, but we walked everywhere.This location is very close to the Louvre and one block off the Jardin de Tuilleries.

<Author>Lawz333
<Content>Fantastic hotel + location Love this hotel. Cannot really fault this hotel in any major way.GREAT (with emphasis) location. 2 min to the metro and 5 min to the Louvre gardens. A bit hard to find the hotel for taxis and drivers given that it is located in one of the backstreets - but don't let that deter you. The rooms are not massive. However, as you can see in the photos posted on here - it's very modern and comfortable. If you are not into the old classicial french style and prefer to modern touch, then this is the place to be.Great bathroom with separate shower and tub, and bulgari toilettries add an extra touch.Extra chocolate is provided with the turndown service - YUM.There are two lifts in the hotel - can only fit around 5 or 6 ppl at a time, but shouldn't be an issue.I recalled from other reviews that there maybe some issues with the rooms located at the higher floors (with the height of the ceilings). However, as I stayed in level 1 (facing the courtyard), there were no issues. Have recommended this hotel to my friends for their honeymoon and they loved it as well. It is definitely more reasonably priced compared to others in the same area (eg. Westin, Park Hyatt) and provides the same benefits in terms of convenience.Oh, if you have a chance, visit Angelina for brekkie or afternnoon tea. They are the best for hot chocolates and its also 2 min from the hotel on the main road!

<Author>HVB
<Content>Housekeeping was the only weak link My husband and I stayed for almost a week in November during the transit strike. We were extremely grateful the hotel was in a perfect location as we could not use the metro. The hotel staff was great, arranging a driver (with awesome car) to meet us at the airport to avoid long taxi lines. My husband also arranged with the concierge Xavier for us to have a couples massage upon landing. It was probably the best massage I've had. The steam room was a delightful treat and a great way to end a long day of walking. Xavier recommended several excellent restaurants. We ate at L'Ardoise down the block once. Our favorite meal of the trip was at Le Saut du Loup. We had room 201 and I thought the size was plenty. Yes the shower door is typical European and water gets on the floor. Just don't leave anything that can't get wet on the floor. My only gripe with the hotel was housekeeping did not clean our room one day and we had to call for more toilet paper as it was not replenished. The staff were all very nice and helpful. As with many others, we used Marriott points for the stay and paid the extra supplement.

<Author>HoustonLawyer
<Content>Mixed Feelings The Good: the rooms are nice, trendy and upscale, but small. The location is close to Place Vendome, and in a quiet side street so noise is limited. Price for the rooms tend to be very good for what you get - in the 300 Euro range. The Bad: no hot water in the shower at 1pm on a Saturday afternoon. The Ugly: the hotel accidentally gave away our reserved taxi to another guest during the strike, and so my wife and I missed our trainto London. That said, they acknowledged their mistake, and put us up for free that night so we could take the first train in the morning. Overall, lots of plus points, with a few negatives.

<Author>bagsalwayspacked
<Content>A Lovely City Hotel in a Perfect Location! IntroWe decided to spend a relaxing week within walking distance of the Louvre, drsay, the Orangerie and the Rodin museums, and this hotel has the perfect location. We would like to thank the manager, Mr. Perrin, and his fine staff for a memorable stay. The concierges, Olivier, David and Xavier, made our stay even better. Size and quality of the roomsMany reviews have mentioned the size of the rooms; we found them to be typical of other large city hotels. Our first three nights were spent in Room 504 with a small balcony facing Rue Mont Thabor, a quiet street one short block from the Rue di Rivoli and the Tuillierres Gardens. The queen bed was luxurious, and the speedy Internet service was worth 15 E a day to stay in touch with the office. It is a good idea to upgrade to a large room if you can not handle small spaces or if you are accustomed to large spaces and spend a lot of time in the room.Our last four nights were in a larger Room 508, which had a king bed and two double balcony doors facing Rue Alger. My husband had a cold, and it was a great place to spend a good part of the day resting. The selection of TV channels was superb; we enjoyed listening to shows from Dubai and in so many languages. We slipped our iPod into the radio and listened to music each day and read the Wall Street Journal, Herald Tribune and USA Today provided free in the lobby. Many guests have mentioned the fine Bulgari toiletries; we also liked the large, comfortable bath towels and friendly housekeepers who did not knock when we chose to sleep during the day. The room fridges were great for storing jars of yogurt and drinks we purchased at a convenience store about two blocks away on Rue Honore, which was a great place to stroll. Our laptop just fit in the closet safe, where we stored our other valuables when we were out of the room.Hotel facilitiesThe health club/spa downstairs looked wonderful, but we were too tired to use it after so much walking. The After the Rain spa services were inviting but too expensive for our budget at 120E for a one-hour massage. There were free beverages in the lobby and a nice living and reading room for lounging on sofas. The lobby bar was inviting and a good source of glasses of ice for our room. Hotel restaurantEach morning we had breakfast in Pinxo off the lobby; the omelets were tasty, and the selection was wonderful. The fresh sliced kiwi and French yogurt in glass jars were first class. We were spoiled by the fine breakfasts, which were included in our room package. We did not have other meals at the hotel because there are so many highly rated restaurants in the neighborhood.Where to eat nearbyWe relied on the paperback reat Eats in Paris,?and found superb food and service for about 30E per person or less without wine, which usually ran about 15E for a half bottle. Two of our favorites were a block from the hotel, Lrdoise and Le Souffle. With a large, late breakfast, we found that one other meal a day was more than enough. It was a pleasant way to celebrate our tenth anniversary and my husband first trip to Paris.Museums, museums and more museumsThis location was perfect for walking to museums each day. We did not bother with the Metro or buses, and only took taxis when we had walked too far. We recommend the Teaching Company lecture courses on the Louvre and the Impressionists before you visit Paris. They suggest spending only an hour or two looking at a few works of art in each museum in order to avoid burnout. This was a totally different approach from our previous European trips, and it worked superbly. There is too much to see in a week in Paris, so just select a few places and enjoy a small part of them at a relaxed pace. Other sightsWe enjoyed a day walking to St. Chapelle and Notre Dame and touring the two islands in the Seine. Another day we visited the Arc de Triumphe and walked along the Champs and to the Eiffel Tower. The Peugeot store on the Champs had the latest concept cars and cool tee shirts from the rugby championships the company was sponsoring in Paris this year. The restaurants and shops along Rue Marbeuf are first class. La Fermette de Marbeuf is a jewel not to be missed. Rick Steve aris 2008?came in handy for guiding us through the sights. There is so much to see that we could spend at least another year in Paris and not return to any place twice. We had no problem communicating with our meager 100 word French vocabularies.The neighborhoodWelcome to heaven! Besides the unbelievable museums a few minutes away, the Westin, the Ritz, the Meurice and many upscale shops are within a block or two of the Renaissance. W.H. Smith offers English books, and Angelina has the world famous hot chocolate. The Tuilleries Gardens are delightful for people watching. SummaryIf you are looking for a quiet, relaxing vacation in central Paris, this hotel is the best. The room sizes and prices are appropriate for this neighborhood. Marriott has done a fine job decorating and staffing this Renaissance, and we truly enjoyed our stay.

<Author>Muscae
<Content>Great little hotel, but snooty service Renaissance Vendome is beautifully decorated, with very plush rooms: marble bathroom outfitted with Bulgari Green Tea toiletries; flat-screen TV, high thread count sheets. The location is lovely, too: just off the Place Vendome in the rue St Honore shopping district, and five minutes to metro Tuileries or walking distance to the Louvre if you're wearing flats. It's tucked away on a side street, so it's quiet and feels very intimate.The only downside is that the service doesn't feel very caring. I'm a Platinum member at the Marriott hotels, but received only a free breakfast: no cocktails, no internet access, no welcome drink. At breakfast, we were ignored by the staff until we literally had to peek into the kitchen to seek service. There was a false fire alarm at 10am on Sunday, and the staff didn't even bother to explain what was happening although guests were trooping down to the lobby in their bathrobes.Likewise, the concierge was not at his desk when I inquired about restaurant reservations. The receptionist literally said, It's not my job, before reluctantly helping me to call the restaurant. In the end, the concierge did return and did his job well, securing the booking and dialing my overseas mobile phone to confirm the booking with me; but it felt rather flat by that point.

<Content>Wonderful hotel. This was a wonderful hotel. We had less than two full days in Paris, so I was really looking for a good hotel. This one was great. I had never been to Paris before, and with such a short amount of time, location was important. This was right up the street from the Louvre and within walking distance of many other sites. The bed was incredibly comfortable. Breakfast was included, but we did not get it as we wanted to be out and about. We did get coffee sent up to the room each morning.  We would definately stay at this hotel again!

<Author>chrisjo06
<Content>Renaissance Paris Vendome, tres bon! My wife and I stayed at the Renaissance Paris Vendome for 3 nights to celebrate our wedding anniversary. Having used some of our Marriott Rewards points to pay for the room (we did pay a 60Euros per night surcharge to upgrade to a prestige room, which was worthwhile doing) it is difficult to comment on value for money. That said the staff, especially reception/concierge were welcoming and knowledgeable. Breakfast (included in the rate) was good enough although we chose to eat other meals in restaurants other than the hotel (Bistrot du Paris, Rue de Lille, was excellent and walkable!). Items in the mini bar were way over priced and, like everywhere in Paris, drinks in the bar were very expensive. The room was spacious enough, quiet and relaxing, very comfortable, LCD TV/DVD player, great bed and a perfectly acceptable bathroom. The location of the hotel is fantastic - we walked to e.g. the shopping area(s), Le Louvre, the Eiffel Tower, Tuiliants, St.Germain, etc. Would we stay there again? Definitely.

<Author>DCDaveBrad
<Content>I've stayed at the best...and this is better! There's a reason this hotel spent years ranked in Trip Advisor top 20 out of 1700 hotels in Paris and it belongs back there. I don't know at what other hotels the people who gave this one bad marks have stayed previously, but I've stayed at Ritz Carltons, Fairmonts and The Breakers in Palm Beach and the service, facilities, and accommodations at this hotel are on par with, if not better than, the best of these.As others have reported, the hotel is in a beautiful building on a nice, quiet street one block off the Rue de Rivoli. The location is amazing! We were five minutes from the Louvre or the Champs Elysees, two minutes from the Tuilleries Garden and its Metro station, and within easy walking distance dozens of great cafs, including Caf Angelina with the best hot chocolate on the planet, not to mention the fun and friendly Carr Irish Pub across the street! The dcor is warm and inviting and the staff is friendly and efficient. We had decided to upgrade to a eluxe?room and it was a good move. Was the room a bit small by American standards? Yes, but Ie stayed in smaller and this one was quite comfortable, with plenty of closet and storage space in the nice, wood wall units. There was ample room to move around, and the flat screen TV was very cool, especially with the DVD/CD player hooked into it (I could play my CDs through the TV!). Also, it was really nice having windows that opened, but they also sealed up tight and the double-paned glass did a great job keeping out what little noise there was. We also loved the queen-sized bed, from the foam pillows we requested in advance to the ust right?mattress to the soft, cozy comforter. I usually don sleep well in hotels, but I slept great in this one!Ie read the comments about the showers, and this would be the only thing I might be tempted to complain about. I confess I not clear on why they wouldn just put in a shower curtain or a full glass door on the tub, but I assuming there a good reason. However, the bathroom was very nice and we adapted to the situation with very little effort. My wife decided to take a bath instead of a shower each morning while I shaved, and when it was my turn, we just put down the bath mat and her towel and that pretty much kept the floor dry (the towels are so huge, it covered half the floor anyway!). This was a very minor inconvenience and we were not bothered by it at all.The service was excellent. We took advantage of the free breakfast every morning, ordering pretty much whatever we wanted, and our meal was delivered promptly every morning at the time we specified the night before. We had a little trouble adjusting the A/C (which we needed because it was unseasonably warm the week we were there), but one call to the front desk took care of that. And, the concierge was very helpful, obtaining our museum passes for us and steering us to a nearby abac?for the phone card we needed. And, the icing on the cake for this hotel is the pool! In a beautiful room decorated with tile and teak wood, it was actually a bit larger than I expected. It even has those big water ets?at one end so you can swim toward them and it like youe swimming laps without moving! Not that we were looking to exercise at the end of the day! The pool was the perfect way to relax after several hours of walking and admiring the sights and if you stay here, definitely take advantage of it.Location, amenities, service, comfort, this place has it all. The Renaissance is an outstanding hotel that will help make your special trip to Paris even more so. We will definitely stay there again.

Not once did we enter/leave the hotel without one of the doormen opening the door and wishing us a smiling bonjour or bon nuit. I have to say -- our stay at the Renaissance Vendome was even more enjoyable than any of our previous stays. My wife and I are already planning to return here next year.

<Author>Escaramujo
<Content>Location, location, location 10 years a go I stayed a week on my honeymoon on the Marriott Champs Elysses (a gift from my father in law) and promised my wife that one day I would take her back there . 10 years later, in a much better economic shape, we went back. I had accumulated Marriot Rewards Points and decided to use them in Paris to fulfill my promise. Being both the Rennaissance Paris Vendome and the Marriott Champs Elysses category 7 hotels (Marriott ratings) I decided on the Renaissance after reading reviews here and listening to friends that have stayed in both.I was shocked when I entered the hotel. This one does not have the glamour, luxury or size of the Marriott and thought I had made a huge mistake. But to tell you the truth, this hotel grew on me, and at the end of my stay I could say that I will definitevely go back to this one as oppose to the Marriott. The reason: LOCATION, LOCATION, LOCATION. Probably the best location in Paris, near everything (we like walking as oppose to taking the Metro) as other comments mention. If you need the Metro is 2 blocks away. If you want to walk, this is near everything. Our room was very small (the size of a cruiseship room, but with a much better bathroom), but was cozy, modern and impecable. Great bed, great shampoo, lotion and soap (Bulgary), an electric towel warmer and super giant brand new towels, a LCD (Sony) TV hanged in the wall and sheets+conforter that you dont want to get out of bed (You have to though, you are in Paris). Personel is ok, nothing extraordinary but works ok. I used the swimming pool one day just for curiosity after a long day of walking (10 hours) and was pleasently surprised (a little cold though). It is small but very modern. Did not eat brakfast in the hotel. Who needs eggs, toast,etc, while there are great boulangeries and coffee everywhere? So this is my advice: Dont get turn down by your first impression of this small boutique type hotel. It has everything you need in a Perfect Location.

<Author>retrac5
<Content>Centrally located - worked perfectly for us We loved this hotel - not perfect, but perfect for us. Here are some details. Our stay: 2/18/07 - 2/24/07Booking: Very easy - we used Marriott Reward PointsLocation: Excellent. A VERY short walk (5 minutes) from the Tuileries Metro station and only 10 minutes to the Louvre, 15 minutes to the D'Orsay, 45 minute walk up the Champs-Elysees to the Arc, about the same to the Eiffel Tower. Every thing could be walked to within one hour - but the easy Metro Access gave us many choices and the RER station at the D'Orsay gave us direct access to Versaille as well. ***Warning - the Metro ticket machines do not accept American Credit Cards or paper euros. If you plan to use the machine, bring coins. ****Warning #2 - the Tuileries metro ticket window was not open on Saturday morning at 7:30AM when we were leaving for the airport (CDG) - so without enough coin change, we were unable to buy tickets directly to the airport. It required exiting the system while still within zone 1 (which is all the change we had) to buy tickets to the airport from a staffed ticket booth.Check-in: Wonderful. Staff was very pleasant and had our room ready when we arrived at the hotel shortly after 12 Noon. Room: As advertised in other postings, a little small. Very nice, very modern (flat screen); but limited drawer space. Our room was on the first floor with a balcony to an interior courtyard. Very Quiet. Bathroom: Very nice, but again, as other postings have stated - the shower leaks a lot. This could be solved rather easily in my opinion by putting a flange on the bottom of the door to capture and redirect water back into the shower instead of allowing it to fall outside the door onto the bathroom floor. Smoked glass bathroom doors (both from the room and to the shower and toilet provide little privacy when the lights in the bathroom are on. There is enough ambient light though from the room, so when we wanted privacy, we just left the bathroom light off.Service: Excellent. If we left the Privacy sign on the door, we were left alone; even when we forgot, they always knocked and made sure that it was OK to come in. When we were out, the room was cleaned quickly and well; regardless if we had left the Privacy sign out all day and removed it at 6PM. Even at that hour they cleaned without our request. Nightly turn down service was also provided (when the Privacy sign was not on the door) with tasty chocolate suckers brought to the room.Price: As mentioned, we booked the room with Marriott Reward points, however, we upgraded to the Deluxe Room - which provided a larger room and a full breakfast for 3 of us each day. The charge for this upgrade was 60euro per day, which we considered reasonable.Restaurant: Breakfast - Wonderful - eggs to order or scrambled eggs, sausages, bacon, toast, fruit, cheeses, sliced meats - we ate there everyday (to take advantage of our deluxe upgrade).Dinner - Very popular and the menu looked good, but the one night that we decided to eat there for dinner, there were no reservations available. This was fortunate for us as the Concierge recommended a wonderful neighborhood restaurant only 5 minutes walk down the same street - which served great food and even better atmosphere.Excercise Room, Spa, Pool - very nice. In the basement and underutilized. We enjoyed a relaxing swim and sauna.Overall - perfect for us. We would love to be pampered at the Four Seasons, but can't afford that type of experience (yet). This hotel had very friendly staff, a comfortable bed, and was a GREAT LOCATION for touring. We would definitely return to this hotel!

<Author>jwbiv
<Content>Very disappointing, so many better choices in Paris After having read the reviews here, we were looking forward to a great experience at this hotel, but what a joke. While one reviewer wrote the rooms are small, but this is Paris,, after having stayed in more than a dozen other hotels in Paris, many less than half of the price of this one, I can honestly say this was the tiniest hotel room I ever had. At these prices, there is simply no excuse.Yes, the location is terrific -- and that's important because you certainly can't stay in your room. There is also no place to unpack (no drawers, horrible use of space), and not even enough room to keep your suitcase on a rack.Second day there we awoke to no electricity in our room. We finally got reception to pick up the phone, and were told they'd get back to us. A half an hour later someone showed up, said they hadn't realized whole block of rooms were without power (and air circulation) but they were getting it back on. There was never the slightest apology about this.The concierge is a waste -- the only bad meal we had in Paris was his recommendation, and the breakfast in the hotel, at 29 Euros, is insane -- and not much too it. There are numerous cafes in the area, while also pricey, offer a decent petit dejeuner for around 10 Euros instead.We used Marriott points so shouldn't complain this much, but friends stayed there as well and they were really ripped off.Believe me, we stayed at a hotel for half the price on the Left Bank, had a sense of true Paris, great, large room, with a view, impeccable service -- and the room rate was less than half of this.Don't settle for an inferior experience -- if you are only comfortable in chain hotels, Westin around the corner and the Hilton on the left bank (where rooms are also twice the size) are far superior choices. A horrible experience...

<Author>mandbear
<Content>You can't go wrong! Beautiful Hotel Great Location!!! Located one block from the Tuileries Metro and just about everything is walking distance, including the Louvre and the Champs Elysees. The hotel is tucked away on a very quiet street and the beds were heavenly, so every night was a very peaceful sleep. The pool was very cozy. After a long day of sightseeing, it's a great place to unwind with a glass of wine (that I would recommend buying at a little grocery store if you walk by one. You can buy a wonderful bottle for less than $10.) Bundle up if you go in the winter. It was cold and cloudy but oh so beautiful with the Christmas trees and the lights. This is a great hotel for married couples traveling alone, although I'm sure it's good for children as well. Oh, one other thing, we were there on Christmas Eve and Day and they brought us a box of German chocolate cookies. They were so good and I thought that was very kind of them. By the way, if you travel during the holidays and are fearing that nothing will be open, do not worry. Most all of the museums were open on Christmas Eve, including the Louvre and the Eiffel Tower is open on Christmas Day. We had no problem finding restaurants either. Sadly, everything was open, but that was great for us hungry tourists. I HIGHLY recommend Rick Steve's Paris 2007 guide. Rick Steve's is the best guide book writer ever.

<Author>karl_H11
<Content>Absolutely Mediocre Hotel, But Decent Location Nice staff, close proximity to many major Paris attractions and conevenient to Metro. Common areas are comfortable and clean, but the rooms are not. I switched rooms three times for reasons ranging from gnats to dirty bathrooms. As it is, the room I settled for wasn't much better than those I abandoned. The majority of the bathroom floor tiles were cracked, the grout on the bathroom floor was virtually gone, there was flaking paint surrounding the bath ceiling light fixtures, flaking paint above the vanity, and the shower was down right dirty (black crud in the corners and in the grout). The reading light on one side of the bed was hanging by its wires and there was a film of dust on the shelf. Housekeeping is not a priority at this hotel. Given that this hotel went through a recent renovation, it's a shame that it isn't maintained well. In my disgust with my accommodations, I sought out other hotels in the same price range, but sadly have to say that this hotel was the lesser of the evils. I will return to Paris, but I won't return to this hotel. I'll probably have to spend more in order to find a hotel that has better upkeep, but so be it. It's frustrating to spend alot of money and not be happy with one's accommodations. This hotel, in my opinion, really needs to crack down on housekeeping.

<Author>Nick_UK-7
<Content>Great 4 star experience in Paris We booked the Renaissance Vendome on a Mariott Magic 1-2-3 promotion (stay over the weekend for and get 25% off the second night). Having stayed in Paris before we knew that 4 star quality could be variable, and wholeheartedly enjoyed the Vendome!Location is great, 10 minutes walk from the Opera and five minutes to the Louvre and Tuileries. The hotel resides in a quite street with minimal traffic. We stayed in a deluxe room on the 5th floor and had no noise issues whatsoever. Our friends stayed on the 1st floor and had no complains either.The hotel was recently refurbished. Modern room decor, curtains, bathroom with Bvlgari perfumed shower products, the bed all were exceptional. In fact closer to a 5 star level, not to mention fitness centre with pool in the basement. The size of the room was totally consumed by the enormous (Queen) bed. The room could have been larger, but we have seen much smaller ones as well.The service was typical laid back French and required some getting used to, but overall the stuff was very friendly and trying hard to be helpful - one of the better examples we have seen.Overall, it's no Bristol or George V, but a great 4 star in the heart of le Grande Bulevards and I have no problems recommending it!

<Author>mbcjim
<Content>Very nice I just spent 3 nights at the Renaissance Vendome and was pleased with the entire experience. The top floor room (6th floor) was luxurious and faced the inner courtyard, easily the quietest room I have ever had in a big city. It was small, not the type of room to comfortably spend the day lounging around in, but who would want to do that in Paris? Breakfast was included in my rate (about $265 per night) and was a basic European Marriott type buffet served in the Pinxo restaurant. I did not try the restaurant in the evening, but I loved ending my long days of trekking about Paris by relaxing with a cigar and a drink in the bar just off the lobby. Pretty pricey, but friendly service and interesting fellow travelers to converse with made it a good value. The pool, sauna, steam room and exercise room are located on the floor beneath the lobby and are another nice way to end a busy day. The staff all spoke English and were polite and helpful. I might go back just for the nouget candies on the front desk!

An estate agent might describe these rooms as intimate, if you know what I mean.2) Price: you expect pricey food, drinks, broadband, and all that kind of stuff, but not this pricey, which reminds me - if you do fancy a pint in the Irish pub across the road be aware that they'll charge you a jaw-dropping ? a beer.3) TV: you only get four english language channels (Sky News, CNN International, BBC World and Bloomberg - and really, who cares about Bloomberg!), and half the time we've been here they've either been totally unavailable or subject to cuts in transmission.Dissapointing really: 2 out of 5. I'd recommend the larger suite at the Hotel du Louvre - great value for money.

<Author>LisaUSA
<Content>Magnificent Hotel!!!! I cannot disagree more with the previous review! It was perfect in every way. The hotel looks exactly the same as the photos. From the minute you arrive, the staff tries to please. They are happy young and professional; they smile. They recommend restaurants, tours, etc. They will clean your room at 6pm when you forget to take the do not disturb sign off your door. The room, while cozy, was not too small. It was spotless. It overlooked a quaint street with an Irish Cafe on the corner. It was not too loud. I was compelled to people watch between 1 and 3 am when jet lag kept me up. One thing I could not figure out was how come the people pouring out of there at that time looked so sober. We got an awesome deal directly from the Renaissance web site (Pure Magic package). I was going to stay at the Ritz or FS, but I just could not part with 1000 bucks a nite. We got a room for 299 E per nite, breakfast included, with the third nite 50% off. The breakfast was delicious. Croissants, pain au chocolate, fresh fruit, cereal, yogurt, etc. We had room service one nite, very expensive (hamburger and fries 21E), food ok, hit the spot.Pool, sauna, steam room and fitness room were top-notch. we used them every day after our touring. They have a library where coffee, tea, etc are available during the day. The location was perfect for us. It is right across the street from the Louve. This hotel has it all!

<Author>Ghostie
<Content>Lovely hotel We had a wonderful stay in this hotel. We arrived off the Eurostar quite early and took a taxi to the hotel, hoping that we could drop off our luggage and then check in later. Even though we were early, the hotel found us a room which was lovely. In addition to the some of the traveller photos, we had a separate walk-in shower.The only downside of the hotel was the restaurant. We came back having walked all over Paris during the day, and just wanted an easy meal without having to set out again. The hotel's restaurant is Japanese style and seemed very stylised, rather than offering the sort of food we wanted. In the end we headed over to Carr's and had a meal there, which was nice, but quite expensive.The other recommendation that we'd make is to bring your fitness and swimming gear. We didn't - but checked out the pool and gym and they looked great. We would definitely bring our stuff with us the next time we visit.The best thing about the hotel is it's location - it's so central and yet very quiet. We loved it and would definitely stay here again.I would reiterate some of the comments about the prices charged by the hotel. We were waiting for a taxi to go back to Gare du Nord and ordered two coffees in the lobby - this came to about 25 euro, which I thought was excessive.There's so much to see and do in Paris that we didn't spend enough time in the hotel, but it's a great base to have for your stay.

<Author>LossForAName
<Content>Pleasantly Predictable--with just the right amount of Parisian Charm We just returned from a week at the Renaissance Paris Vendome (RPV). There were many highlights--and a few things that could be improved. Even factoring in the problems, we judged the overall quality of our stay as excellent--but, of course, that depends on individual expectations.A few comments:LOCATION, location, location. . .It's hard to get much better than Mont Thabor--a relatively quiet street just off the Rue du Rivoli and extremely accessible to most of the must see sights in the city. A brief warning: the restaurant and bar across the street can get a bit noisy for the rooms on the street side. IT'S A MARRIOTT. . .Which means that you can get a true non-smoking room--something possessed by only 1/2 of the Top 6 hotels in the 1st arrondissement (as reported by the 2006 Michelin Red Guide) . I started sneezing the moment I stepped into DeGaulle Airport from all of the cigarette smoke and was greatly appreciative of a well-ventilated, smoke-free place to sleep. It also means that standard business services (like high speed Internet) are available--although at a price. It also means that you can get Marriott points for the large amounts you are bound to spend (the current exchange rate from $ to euros is miserable). Finally, the clientele is principally American, which may be good or bad, but does mean that the staff speaks excellent English and is used to dealing with American eccentricities and handles them graciously.PINXO. . .Is the RPV's onsite restaurant and is run by a genuine Michelin 2-star chef , although Pinxo has yet to garner a rating of its own. The speciality of Pinxo is southwestern French regional cuisine served as small plates and presented in 3 portions to encourage sharing, although sharing seemed to be at a minimum when we ate dinner there. (I understand that sharing typically is not done in France, although we did not hesitate.) The food was excellent and a nice break from traditional (rich) French cuisine; the service was attentive; and the wine list had a number of wines priced at 25 euros a bottle--which made for a reasonably affordable dinner. At breakfast, the Pinxo dining room doubles as the hotel's breakfast room, with a fairly pricey, unmemorable buffet and indifferent service. If breakfast is included in your room rate--terrific. If not, make other plans.ROOMS. . .Yes, they are small, but they are extremely clean, comfortable, secure and very well-appointed. They come off a bit as a room you would find at a W hotel in the states--but in miniature. One beef was a voicemail light on the phone that the staff (despite 4 requests) couldn't seem to get to fully turn off in any consistent manner. I finally gave up and left a message for callers not to trust the voicemail and to have the receptionist hand-deliver messages--which was done in a timely fashion. A complimentary bottle of water comes with the room, but it is only a single bottle for an entire stay. They can do better here. (I would trade the designer chocolates provided every evening for a bottle of water, although I'm not certain everyone would agree with me.)BATHROOMS. . .The bathrooms were nice, although tiny, with extra soft towels and the promised Bulgari amenities. However, I often wonder why the hotels that provide the most upscale amenities don't provide conditioner (for instance, the Carlyle in NYC provides Kiehl products, but no conditioner). In any event, if you use conditioner bring your own or plan to visit a drugstore. Also the glass half-shade on the tub generally results in at least some water landing on the bathroom floor--particularly when the chambermaid leaves the shower head pointing directly out into the bathroom, as occurred on one occasion. The final beef on the bathroom front: although the shower always had great water pressure, the heat of the water could sometimes be a bit uneven.CONCIERGE. . .The concierge desk was always staffed with helpful personnel and we were delighted to find out that they had museum passes available for sale. The point of museum passes for us was not so much to save money as to save time. Our passes helped us skirt long lines at the Louvre, d'Orsay and l'Orangerie, so we could spend more time enjoying Paris. The concierge also sends out a helpful email in advance of your stay. ALEXANDRA. . .My husband would consider this review to be lacking if I didn't put in a nice word for the RPV's tiny, elegant little bar and Alexandra, who staffed it most nights we stopped by. For something different, do try a custom infused cocktail using the sticks on the bar--it's even a concept you can bring home to show your guests something new and different you learned in Paris. SOME FINAL SIGHTSEEING NOTES. . .Do plan to go up to Montmartre. While some of the guidebooks made us question whether it was worth our while, it definitely was. We took the metro up to Place Pigalle, did the obligatory trek to Sacre Coeure and then just enjoyed wandering around the area, chatting with street artists and seeing the sights. We did not tour Pig Alley, which is reputed to be rife with pickpockets and which signs at the metro warn the unsuspecting about. It is a fairly easy walk (downhill) from Montmartre back to the 1st arrondissement. One RPV reviewer mentioned the Batobus, which is a form of public transportation on the Seine. It is a very efficient way to get a quick lay of the land--take a trip early on your visit. A special thanks to that reviewer for suggesting it.

<Content>Great Place My husband and I stayed here for our honeymoon and were nicely surprised how nice the hotel is. I found the receptionists to be very helpful and professional. On arrival our receptionist informed us at check-in that as a honeymoon couple they were giving us a free bottle of champagne and free breakfast during our stay. We used the safe and found it to be useful to store our valuables. The breakfast is definitely worth the visit as it was buffet style and closes at 10:30am. We enjoyed our breakfast thoroughly every morning and ordered room service if we missed it while room service for breakfast ends at noon. The hotel is very close to all the attractions and the Metro is only a few blocks away. I would highly recommend staying. Our flight was to leave late on our last day, so the receptionist said they would allow us to keep our room for longer if the hotel was not booked to capacity. Unfortunately it was but they were more than willing to store our luggage until we left. The swimming pool was nice and quite big and the sauna couldn't have been hotter. <Author>RusNewton
<Content>Very nice hotel.... but.... I took my family and parents to Renaissance Paris Vendome for a week. We had three rooms. The hotel is very nice, the staff were friendly and accommodating but I came away feeling nice, but.. when I compare it with stays at other five-star hotels. On the nice side were the gym and swimming pool, both of which appeared very new, were not at all crowded (in fact most of the time we were the only ones in the pool which was lovely), with decent locker-rooms and showers. Flat-panels in all the rooms, and DVD players (but no evidence of a menu of DVDs to borrow although I didn't look that hard because we were out all the time so we didn't need in-room entertainment). Beds were very comfortable, with a very nice topper on the matress which is not that common but gives a luxury feel.On the but side: 1. We asked for interconnecting rooms so my kids (aged 6  8) could have their own room but get to us easily. We were initially given rooms separated by two other rooms - when we complained, we were moved to adjoining but not interconnecting rooms after one night. Not the end of the world, but even so annoying.2. The bath robes were regularly removed from the room and not replaced, which was a bit annoying given we didn't have interconnecting rooms so if the kids wanted us in the middle of the night it is kind of handy to have a robe to put on when you step into the corridor. We asked repeatedly and eventually got robes but again, annoying to have to ask.3. The one and only PC with internet connection in the lobby was out of action for our entire stay4. One of the two lifts was out of action for most of our stay, meaning some competition with the bell-boys for elevator space5. We asked for a taxi to collect us from Gare du Nord so we didn't have to sweat in line after a 3 hour train ride. This is a ten euro trip, but the hotel wanted me to pay 120 euro for their driver to collect us. I consider that an insult when the total budget for the week was already close to ten thousand euro.6. Similarly, babysitting at 30 euro an hour plus 30 euros for taxi home is a rip-off: even the Biltmore in Miami which is a very expensive hotel, offers better value babysitting than that.7. Breakfast was very expensive and they didn't seem to offer any reduction for children: both Le Meridien and Four Seasons typically offer children much cheaper breakfast than 29 euro.So, we had a nice week but it could have been just that little bit better -- and when you book five star, you expect the best, not second best.  
<Date>Jul 21, 2006

<Author>Nutty_663rd
<Content>Quiet hotel with good central location My wife and I have just returned from a 3 night stay in this hotel. We stayed in a prestige room, for which we paid 380 Euros a night, with breakfast included.The Room------------We were initially located room 101 overlooking the street, but because we and they couldn't get into the room safe, we were immediately transferred to room 314, overlooking the central courtyard. The rooms weren't as small as I was expecting given some of the comments in the reviews I'd read before flying out to France, although talking to the receptionists, they did say that some of the prestige rooms were smaller than the others. Room 314 was slightly smaller than room 101, but it had the advantage of a separate shower and bathtub, which room 101 didn't have.Rooms are well appointed, with an LCD style TV, DVD player, King sized bed, air conditioning, well stocked minibar, iron, good bathroom (but as reported before with frosted glass doors so not maximum privacy) and robes/slippers. The bed was very comfortable as was the bedding, with plenty of pillows. However be aware that in both prestige rooms we saw the King sized beds are in fact 2 single beds with single mattresses pushed together, so not a true King bed. Overall though we liked the room and it was perfect for our needs. I think they're better geared towards tourists than business travellers as the desk was small, but in future we'll choose a smaller room because we don't think, for the little time we spent in our room, that it was worth 380 Euros a night.A few grumbles about the room before I move on ....1.) The new safe was on the top shelf in a cupboard, and therefore we couldn't see into it without standing on a chair. Clearly roomkeeping hadn't done this either as there were 2 whisky bottles on top of the safe.2.) Excessive prices of minibar drinks: 6 Euros for a coke. It's pure greed. If my airline can charge me less than 1 Euro for a coke and make a profit, I don't expect a hotel to keep on this sort of nonsense. We therefore spent no money in the hotel on drinks, although I would have quite happily settled into a few cocktails each evening if I didn't feel that I was being ripped off. After all at 360 Euros a night, something we thought was somewhat excessive for the room size, the hotel could and should be generating a great deal of goodwill by offering drinks to hotel guests at much much cheaper rates. 3.) DVD rental. The LCD TV system doesn't offer movies so the hotel offers DVDs for hire for 10 Euros. I think all hotels could generate a great deal of goodwill if they dropped this stupid nonsense of overcharging for in-room movies.The Staff-----------The staff were all excellent, spoke English well, and were a pleasure to deal with. The Breakfast-----------------We choser to have our included breakfast in our room, for which there is no additional charge, although you're limited to choosing from the continental menu. So it's the usual selection of French pastries, cereals, and fresh fruit salad, which suited us well. However with the location of many cafes and restaurants in the surrounding area, in the future we'd choose to have breakfast away from the hotel. We can't comment on the breakfast in the restaurant as we didn't eat in there.The Pool and Gym---------------------Ok well I don't do gyms, but there were about 8 or so pieces of high end equipment. The pool was excellent - small, but usable to exercise in and cool off. The pool has two adjustable underwater jets for those of us who like to exercise against a current. Wonderful! A very classy pool with slate and wooden surroundings. Note that whilst you can turn the jets on or off, they can be very powerful, and so children shouldn't be allowed to use them without supervision. As well as the pool and gym, there's a boiling steam room (the hottest I've ever experienced) and a sauna, plus shower. Location----------I agree with everything that everyone else has said about this hotel's location. A quiet street, in a lovely area of Paris, within a short walking distance to great shopping, sight seeing and famous landmarks. This is a perfect part of Paris to stay in.Would we return?---------------------Probably, if we could get a better rate. For my money, the hotel's location, and the ability to have a swim at the end of a day's walking and shopping, are what will bring me back to this hotel, but as a said, so long as we can secure a better rate!  
<Date>Jul 11, 2006

<Author>AureliaTraveler
<Content>Enjoyed Our Stay We just returned from a trip to France. While in Paris, we stayed at the Renaissance Place Vendome. We had two stays at the hotel, one night before leaving for Provence, and five nights while we explored Paris. We booked a prestige room for the one night stay, and a quality room for the five night stay. The only difference between the two was a little more space, a king sized bed vs a queen sized bed, and a separate tub and shower in the bathroom for the prestige room. Our breakfast at PINXO (the hotel's restuarant) was included for three days. The breakfast is a buffet, and the staff will fix eggs for you, plus bring you coffee, hot chocolate, etc. The buffet consists of cereals, breads, and hams. When breakfast wasn't included, we ate elsewhere. The location is excellent - you are in walking distance of the Louvre, the Orsay, the Place de Concorde and you are in the elite shopping district of Paris. There are plenty of ATMs, restaurants, the Tuilleries Metro stop, and Batobus stop close by. The only downside to the Renaissance is if you want a beautiful view from your room, it isn't available. The hotel is located on a side street.The hotel is very modern and well maintained. We had a very enjoyable and comfortable stay. The staff is very friendly and everyone speaks English. Whatever our request, it was promptly taken care of. I would definately stay at the Renaissance Place Vendome again if I ever return to Paris.

<Content>Great Location in Ritzy Area Very nicely appointed, upscale, modern rooms with flat screen TV, DVD player. The hotel is located on quiet street between Rue de Rivoli and Rue Saint Honore. The bathroom was split in two with toilet and sink on one side of room near the entrance and the shower/main sink on other side of the room. We didn't care much for the frosted glass doors on the bathrooms - felt like a lack of privacy. Definitely recommend if you want a more modern style hotel.

<Author>slickoperator
<Content>Very good hotel but the marketing is skewed This is a very good hotel. It's a modern, recently designed and built establishment in an excellent, central location. You're within 10 minutes' walk of the Louvre and just 15 minutes of the Opera. From that point of view it could hardly be bettered.The service is second to none and the breakfasts are very good. I think breakfast is probably very expensive even by Paris standards, so if you want to save money, you should know that within a few minutes' walk of the hotel there are some very pleasant cafes on the Rue de Rivoli.I booked on the internet and upgraded my booking because I wanted to give my wife a treat. I have to say that I was disappointed on several counts:1. When I arrived the staff appeared unaware of the upgrade or what it entailed;2. The upgrade was supposed to give me a bottle of champagne on arrival, but it was not to be had until asked for;3. The room was small. I think this was the biggest disappointment. If they offer an upgrade for couples I think that the room ought to be a priority - but it was so small that my wife and I had to negotiate verbally before getting out of the bed because there was so little room. The bathroom was almost as big as the bedroom. Furthermore, I'm not pleased that the first thing they said to me when I checked in was that I could upgrade my room for 80 euros. Well, if you've already upgraded your booking, why should you have to upgrade again if you want a decent-sized room?So on balance, this is a very good hotel, but their marketing is, I think, annoyingly skewed. Either you upgrade, and you upgrade properly, getting a decent room, or you don't. It's as simple as that. But to have several layers of upgrade, none of them understood by the staff, seems to me crazy.

<Author>holiday-anyday
<Content>Lovely stay in a lovely hotel Tripadvisor hotel reviews were so helpful in finding accommodations, I have to give back. I booked this hotel for 8 nights in February 2006, based on the reviews in this website. It did not disappoint. My husband and I stayed in a Deluxe room on the sixth floor, overlooking the small courtyard. We did not have any problems with the ceiling height - it was a uniform height throughout. The room was quiet, and very dark when the shades were closed, just as we like it. We were surprised to learn that internet access is not free, but when we informed the front desk that our reservations indicated it was included, they waived the charges. The location is in a pricey, higher-end section of Paris, but conveniently located. The concierge was very helpful making restaurant reservations before and during our stay. Since the restaurants were ones I requested, I did not have the opportunity to try any that the concierge may recommend. My husband's luggage was delayed for 2 days en-route from Italy, and the concierge helped track its status and ensure it was delivered to our room. We used the pool and sauna 3 times, and it was a relaxing way to end the day. Complaints are minor: we did not get turn-down service one night. Drinking water was only provided in the room the day we checked in. The sauna was not turned on one time, and we had to go to the front desk to fetch someone to turn it on (which was controlled in a locked cabinet next to the sauna), and it took so long to heat up that we did not stay. We did not try breakfast at the hotel, although we did enjoy a nice cup of coffee one morning. I would not hesitate to stay here again.

<Author>Leicstourist
<Content>A good hotel This hotel was up to the usual high standard of the Marriott chain. The reason for my interest in the first place was the pool - very unusual for central Paris but such a benefit when travelling with the children. It was small but adequate and we enjoyed the steam room - black slate all round and star effect ceiling! Our rooms were connected by a private door and corridor and overlooked the quiet street outside. Rooms large by Paris standards and the windows opened. Usual very comfortable beds and pillows and standard extras such as dressing gowns and slippers. Excellent bathroom and lovely Bvlgari soaps and lotions. All the staff in the hotel were attentive and welcoming. The location is superb, close to everything. The only downside was the cost of drinks in the bar and especially the cost of breakfast. Service in the bar was very good and maybe justified the price. Service at breakfast did not. The selection for the continental breakfast was thin and at something like 23 euros each was extortionate. For an additional charge you could have the hot buffet which was bacon, sausage and scrambled egg. And, er, thats it. Orders for other eggs were disorganised and long winded. Poached eggs arrived 15 minutes later like hardboiled and cold to boot! And we got another guest's part order! As others have observed you can get a great French breakfast for a fraction of the price a few streets away. But in February when its cold and raining do you really want to put on all the overcoats and trudge through the chill to have breakfast and then trudge back. No, you expect that in the hotel, so thats were you go, especially if you have kids. So much so that I paid 23 euros for 3 croissants, a bit of butter, a bit of jam and some coffee!So for me the only downside was the breakfast issue, otherwise everything else about this hotel was first class and highly recommended over all the others I have stayed at in Paris.And yes the taxi driver will have trouble finding the hotel.Its at the absolute end of Rue du Mont Thabor (which is one way)on the left hand side opposite the Irish pub.Enjoy!

<Author>NorthernSpy
<Content>Worked well for business travel I stayed 4 nights from 11/30 to 12/4 in a prestige room which means you have the option of a king bed. Room faced the inner courtyard/atrium and was very quiet except occasional ka-thumping of other rooms' doors. Bathroom was split with toilet and sink in one small room and at the other end of bedroom, larger area with full tub and vanity. I enjoyed the room and decor very much but this design element was somewhat inconvenient for me. In looking at the floorplan, it appears that most of the rooms are not designed like this. Room was kept spotless during my stay. Staff was helpful without being intrusive. Did not have a chance to sample the pool or spa facilities - maybe next time. I needed internet service and booked this hotel for that reason - service in the room is 19.95 Euros per day- that's not inexpensive and not for the casual user. Did not have a chance to try the wireless in the lobby so I don't know how much that costs. What I used worked flawlessly. Location is excellent for business and sightseeing. I did not have a chance to sample the breakfast but assume something more substantial and less expensive can be easily found nearby. I did have dinner at Pinxo and it was wonderful.
