<Author>Jobster
<Content>A hidden gem I was really worried about booking accommodation in Paris,as I wanted Contemporary, not chintz, I wanted quiet, not noise and I definitely wanted a friendly bar to relax in after a hard days sightseeing!So after lots of research, with trepidation I booked the Renaissance Vendome Plaza...Thank goodness I did.We booked a deluxe room overlooking the courtyard. Whilst small, it had a fantastically huge bed, very modern fittings and fixtures including a plasma telly. The bathroom again very modern, and best of all, no noise !The hotel is situated on a quiet street within a 10 minute walk of the Louvre and 10 mins to Place De Concorde...Walking to the Eiffel Tower via Arc De Triomphes, Champs Elysses etc, was only 30 minutes.The staff in the hotel were excellent. The bar staff were the best I have come across treating me to many cocktails including unusual ingredients such as mint and lemongrass, they made the stay even more memorable.The restaurant attached to the hotel, is fantastic in the evening, but the breakfast was really poor and the staff on the morning shift equally uninterested. I would recommend that should you stay here you turn left out the hotel, then right then left onto the main road towards the Louvre and on your left is a fab cafe serving proper French breakfast rather than hard rolls!Can`t remembe the name but it is in sight of the Palace and opposite a hotel.All in hall I would highly recommend this hotel if you are not looking for Louis style furniture and decor, but instead want modern/ trendy environment. I loved it and without a shadow of a doubt, would recommend it to all my friends and family.A real find in what can be the quagmire of choosing a good Parisian hotel

<Author>TM99
<Content>Perfect Location I have just returned for a business trip to Paris, staying at the Renaissance Paris Vendome; I think it's an excellent hotel. Despite being in Paris on business, the hotel's location meant that I still managed a brief visit to the Louvre and some shopping! The location is absolutely perfect - sandwiched between the Rue de Rivoli (5 mins walk to the Louvre, 10 mins walk to Musee d'Orsay)and the exclusive Faubourg St Honore (a few mins walk to the Opera and the more affordable shops on the Blvd Haussman). The nearest underground is the Tuilieries - 2 mins walk.The hotel itself is boutique style and elegantly appointed. I also liked the fact that this hotel is relatively new and so nothing is worn or shabby. The bedrooms ARE small, but, again, they're well-designed and are very comfortable. It's extremely quiet and I heard no street noise at all. Bathrooms are good with separate shower and bath - plus gorgeous Bulgari toiletries.The swimming pool in the basement is a great asset - when I used it, there was nobody else there and it was most relaxing.I found the service consistently very good and helpful and I had no problems whatsoever with housekeeping or turndown mentioned in some earlier reviews.I would agree that breakfast is very pricey for what is on offer but you are a stone's throw from many other cafes, so that's not a problem. I paid 320 euros/ night for a prestige room, which I believe is very fair for a hotel of this standard in such a location in one of the world's major capital cities.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Quiet, comfortable and friendly, but rather plain and dull If you arrive at the Renaissance Paris Vendome by taxi your driver might have some difficultly finding it; the hotel is tucked away in a small dark back street a block away from the Tuileries. Even the hotel signs are not illuminated, and when I arrived (after eleven) there was no-one at the small entrance. The lobby is no more imposing: it is relatively small and unassuming, although the dark hardwood and stone looks expensive. Still no porter after check-in, but the lift was 5 yards away so I carried my bags to the room with no trouble.I found the room moderately sized; the king bed dominated it, leaving little free floor space. Two built-in wardrobes gave plenty of room and I was pleased to see an iron and ironing board as standard, and off course the two sumptuous dressing gowns neatly folded. The desk had a light and a broadband connection; however the business traveller might find it a little small. Room enough for a laptop and a couple of sheets of paper, but not much more. The hotel must have blessed the invention of the flat screen TV hanging on the wall, because it is hard to see where a decent sized standard set would have gone.The bathroom was somewhat more generously sized. It had both a shower and bath, with separate toilet compartment and was nicely finished in marble, smoked glass and chrome, and spotlessly clean. The shower door seal leaked though (as other reviewers have pointed out) and mopping up after became a daily ritual for us.A worse problem though was to come: before settling down for the night we switched the a/c off to cut out the slight hum that appeared to be coming from it. Strangely, the hum continued. After a bit of investigation we discovered that the main fans for the hotel a/c were situated directly above our room. The noise was not that loud, but it was a bit like being on a George Lucas set with the constant low rumble of a star-destroyer main drive engine in the background. For the real noise though, we could open the room window ?now we get a noise of Ridley Scott proportions from the huge metal cooling duct that runs up the side of the hotel. Admittedly, we did not have much reason to open the window - the view was of a tiny courtyard.In the end though, it was not these things that put me off the hotel. The main disappointment was that the whole place was just too uninspiring. Some people write that it is a ome from home? Well, if I am paying a month mortgage for three days in a room a third of the size of my apartment, I don want to feel at home. I want something a bit swanky. I want guys with hats on the door, a big flashy atrium and some furniture that once belonged to Louis the umpteenth. This is Paris after all, and I want to see something of the glory of France in my hotel. And in case you think this can be found, you need only wander around the corner to see the hotels nearby to see what I mean. Of course, there is the Maurice and the Crillon, for which you will pay more, but you can also find a few grand four stars that look pretty impressive.So, in the end I have to mark this hotel down. True, the staff could not have been friendlier. The spar was nice; I loved the black slate steam room and it is one of the few Paris hotels with a pool (though it is small). But I have to knock a small point off the problems in the room, and a big point off for being too plain, downright dull. A business traveller might find this OK, but if you are going to Paris for that once in a life-time trip, do yourself a favour and splash out a bit extra for a real five star, or save the cash and get a nice four star room with a decent view.Oh - and if you have booked it and your taxi driver asks where this hotel is, tell him it behind the Maurice.

<Author>cheeseburger23
<Content>Utterly comfortable and relaxing We absolutely, hands-down loved this hotel. My husband and I stayed there for a week and a half in September 2005 and can't imagine liking a place better. We enjoy hotels that are high quality, classy, but comfortable and personal. This fit the bill perfectly.Location:If you are touring Paris, the vacation is very central. Right across from the Tuileries, Tuilieries metro stop (on a very central, convenient line), a block from the Louvre, the most wonderful boutiques and shopping right around the corner, restaurants, groceries and cafes everywhere, and yet the hotel is tucked into a side street so it is perfectly quiet. Somebody wrote a review that said there was nowhere to get food nearby. A half a dozen cafes with coffee, croissants, soda, and groceries weren't 20 paces away - they must not have explored thoroughly. Room:We stayed on the 1st floor in room 109. Our room was beautifully decorated with a very contemporary look. The furnishings seemed brand new. A little small, but had ample closet space so once we were unpacked, we had no trouble. We loved to cuddle in bed after a long day of touring and watch our flat screen tv. The bed was a comfy queen. Room was additionally furnished with a desk, desk chair, coffee table and arm chair. We had a bright beautiful window we could open during the day, but we didn't because the weather was around 85 degrees and we wanted to keep the awesome air conditioning running. Room was always flawlessly clean when we arrived back from touring during the day. The bathroom was the only difficulty we experienced, but we were prepared from the other reviews we had. The half glass panel in the shower guarantees a little leakage, but it was easily controlled with spare towels. The bathroom had plenty of counter space and was furnished with robes, a hair dryer, makeup mirror, etc. Toiletries were very nice and yummy smelling.Mini-bar in the room was well-stocked but ridiculously expensive (6 euros for a coke?) There was extra room in the fridge we filled with cheap water and coke from around the corner. The hotel staff didn't seem to mind.Food:We enjoyed room service two evenings which was fast by US standards (15 minutes or less), and ate one night at Pinxo. Food was very high quality and orders were always well understood, including special requests. Many other fantastic restaurants nearby.Spa  Pool:We took advantage of the wonderful spa and pool facilities while we were there, which were very unique for a European hotel. The pool was just as beautiful as it was in the pictures with lots of comfy seats for lounging. The workout room is small but functional, and we both had great massages in the spa area.Language:Everyone we met at the hotel: concierge, room service, spa workers, even cleaning staff had some command of English. While we made our polite efforts in broken French, they had no problem switching to English to help us out.Room would be great for couples, and maybe families who want to take advantage of the pool. We genuinely felt like this hotel was home, and were quite sad to leave its comfortable accomodations. We believe that you'll feel the same!

<Content>Good Service and Location We arrived at about noon on Saturday the 3rd of September and were checked in to our room within ten minutes, a big plus as I had traveled from Los Angeles and just wanted to get some sleep. We had room service that evening, from Pixio(sp?), which was both delivered quickly and very very good - in fact so good that we had dinner at their once during our stay.I found the staff very helpful and friendly and did not experence any delays in getting the room cleaned as had been noted by others. <Author>Irish_JC
<Content>home away from home ! I had originally booked the St Lazare hotel,but based on reviews of the Vendome and guidebooks' comments on the safety around the St Lazare area I decided to change and am so happy I did.This is my 2nd stay in Paris and I am by no means a hotel snob - my normal 3 decision making requirements are - location,safety and quiet.The hotel scores well in all areas.Pros - Location - walking distance from all the sights (except sacre coueur). Perfectly positioned on a quiet side street means you don't hear traffic.(I am a light sleeper so this is a big point for me!)Rooms - big by paris standards. Very well laid out - everything looks and feels new and high quality from the bed to the linen to the desk. LCD tv and dvd player is also great when you get bored of the only 2 english news channels. Bulgari toiletries a nice treat. Bathrooms are nice and big. Broadband access included.bath robes and slippers handy for the pool.Amenities - Pool,sauna,steam room are fantastic after long walks. I only used them one night but we had the pool to ourselves....very nice Staff - Very helpful and pleasant. I didn't bother them too much except for the bill - more on that later. But as others have mentioned they make you feel extremely welcome and I think are the real icing on the cake for this hotel. Bad staff can leave a sour taste in a nice hotel but these guys were great !Cons-location - if you need a quick fix of fruit or bottled water etc,it's quite a walk to find the nearest market. so shop when you're out in the day!the bathroom cannot be kept dry as mentioned previously...annoying maybe,but didn't bother me too muchpool/sauna closes at 10pm...found we were out till that time most nights so would've liked to use it when we came backa couple of other oddities - I received a call from front desk at 7.30am one morning..when I answered they said sorry and hung up....2 bottles of beer appeared on the bill which I didn't have - only thing i can guess is by looking in the minibar they may be scanned and added automatically?the safe was advertised as laptop size but in reality it holds passports and maybe a camera.One reason I enjoyed this hotel so much was that I felt I got a bargain...The rack rate was 269eur but after booking I noticed expedia were offering it at 249.Marriott have a policy of best price which means if you find it cheaper than their site they give you a rate of the lower along with a 25% discount....so my rate was actually 182eur.Front desk hadn't been informed by bookings office,but once I was able to produce the email they were more than happy to oblige.I didn't use restaurant/bar so can't comment.One last recommendation for paris from me is use the Batobus !! 16eur for a 5 day pass - basically a boat along the seine with about 8 stops - hop on,hop off - all the major ones...by far the easiest way to go from champs elysees to eiffel, or eiffel to notre dame - and a great view along the way. the metro means walking,changing lines,not a nice view....boat is superb...runs till 10pm too so you can view the sights at night. only wish i'd discovered it at the beginning of my weekend !I would definitely stay here again - great hotel,location,staff and I would recommend it. you'll feel a little pampered in this home away from home.Deserving of it's high place in ta's customer satisfaction,but it doesn't have the frills of say the beverly hills hotel so I wonder are the people using 5* hotels just more critical?

<Author>ooookch
<Content>Wonderful place - but not perfect There's a lot of good things to say about this hotel, but there are also some downsides. The location is just great, especially if you're into art as Musee d'Orsay and the Louvre are within easy walking distance. The hotel is perfectly styled and has a very nice ambiance, I felt at home immediately. It is also rather quiet, as it is on a back street of the very busy Rue de Rivoli. The room (I had a 'Prestige' room) was not very big, but I loved the extremely comfortable bed, the style and the flatscreen tv. The bathroom however is a typical case of 'design over function', which starts with the doors (which aren't really doors); and as other reviewers mentioned, it is impossible to take a shower without flooding the room. The Bulgari toiletries on the other side are wonderful. Housekeeping was not very good: the room was not ready when I arrived at 5pm and was also made late the next day, the mini bar didn't get refilled, a drinking glass was not cleaned, they knocked at the door once despite the 'do not disturb' sign; all nothing severe but it's not nut truly five star standard. The turndown service however was lovely.The Pool and Hamam are fabulous features after a long day of walking around in Paris, and again with great design. I liked the small but cozy bar. The restaurant is a bit expensive but very good with creative, quite light food. I enjoyed sitting at the marble bar where you can watch the cooks preparing the meals. Breakfast however is hopelessly overprized for the variety and quality of the food offered. I don't mind paying 29 Euro for a breakfast buffet, but for that money I expect more. Go to the Meurice nearby if you want to spend money for breakfast, else there are enough French cafes around to start the day. In addition, staff in the restaurant at breakfast wasn't overly polite and sometimes very stressed, and argued in front of the guests with each other about having too much work to do.Last but not least, the best thing about this hotel is the front desk staff, everybody was extremely nice and helpful. Top notch service!Although there are some little downsides, I rate the hotel with five stars for the style, the staff, the location and the pool, and also because with the exception of the George V all five star places in Paris (including the Ritz and the Crillion) I've tried so far had bigger problems than this one. I'd recommend it to single persons or couples who prefer a stylish, personal hotel over the prestige of the big names.

<Author>Trojan23
<Content>Ideal couples hotel - don't take children Ideally situated in Central Paris in a very quiet street. The Plaza Paris Vendome is not a Hotel aimed at the family market its more of a romantic retreat for adults?it is a real treat. Clean efficient and friendly it has everything you need for a comfortable visit to the French capital. As is the norm in France the rooms are not huge I guess this is just something you have to accept however the rooms are extremely well appointed, with a very comfortable bed  good quality bedding. The small splash screen in the bathroom is only a problem for the hotel staff that come to clean it. In fact we found they would not only clean the bathroom during the day but would do the same again during the turn down service in the evening. The only thing missing was tea  coffee making facilities which was a minor disappointment.The restaurant was very expensive and room service or having a drink in the bar costs far too much, however the number of excellent restaurant within easy walking distance meant we had ample choice and truly good food every day.I think personally think this hotel hits all the right marks that make it deserve it high rating. Highly recommended unless you have kids that is.

<Author>veebrad
<Content>Very disappointed.... I have just returned from Paris. I had spent several weeks researching which hotel to use and I was very influenced by the reviews on the TA website. But I have to confess I was very disappointed in this hotel - by no means a 4-5 star hotel, despite the 5-star price!Its primary benefit is its location which is terrific. But I found it to be deficient in many ways. It is definitely not a family hotel. We travelled with our 11 year old son and had requested a rollaway bed, but the room was so small we could barely get our suitcase in it - to give them credit they did upgrade us to a junior suite! But the room was small - so small thay they didn't have room for a suitcase stand, so we had to park our suitcases in various corners of the floor and dance around them. This may have been the only 5-star hotel I have ever been in that had no clock of anykind in the room - so if, as we did in our jet-lagged state,wake up at night and try to figure what time it was, we had to tip-toe to the bathroom to turn on a light to see - weird, right?Other travellers have commented on the quaint showers. They are not quaint, just downright stupid! The shower is one of those in-tub things but there is not a curtain, just a half-length glass screen, so that when you take a decent-power shower, the water shoots out all over the floor. When you have had to mop up the floor after 3 people have use the shower -every day- and filled the tub with all the soggy towels, this becomes a real pain in the rear after several days. Not to mention the slick floor you have to negotiate afterward- a very user-unfriendly bathroom. I didn't pay these prices to be mopping floors every day !There is a tiny bar, the lobby is cramped and stuffy - Paris was hot when we were there and the lobby air-conditioning was totally inadequate - the room was fine though.We tried the restaurant one night - there was not another customer there. When we looked at the meny we knew why - it was difficult to find anything simple to eat. Everything was sophisticated and expensive - no child-friendly food at all, and this was the only place to eat - so we ate out every night! The downstairs spa/pool area was novel, but I would much prefer a hotel that did better on the basics, than one which had these expensive frills. I cannot recommend this hotel at the price they charge. I was influenced, I must admit, by the hotel we had just stayed in, in London.- the Sofitel St. James. A much more elegant hotel with beautiful big room , exquisite beds, great location - for half the price of our Paris hotel. We loved it!!  
<Date>Jul 6, 2005

<Author>nwillner
<Content>Very nice hotel I'm going to give the Plaza Paris Vendome 5 stars. If there were 4.5 stars I'd actually give that because of just a few hesitations below. There is a great staff (concierges Daniel and Emmanuelle were very helpful), very clean and modern redone rooms, the pool and steam room are fun and different for Paris and the location near the Louvre is great but there are a just a few points that might keep it from 5 star status.The rooms are beautiful but tight even for Europe. (Do go to The Meurice for breakfast 1/2 a block away - like having breakfast at Versailles). The restaurant at the hotel is fantastic and even if we don't stay there next time we'll make a special trip for dinner to Pinxo in the hotel (have the fruit with coconut milk and mint for dessert)

<Author>Holidaymad
<Content>Hotel overbooked!! When we arrived at the hotel on Friday evening we were told that 'a large party had decided to stay an extra night' and that they therefore did not have a room for us - they had instead booked us a room for that night at their sister hotel The Marriott Champs Elysees. The hotel was OK but definately not the quality of the Plaza Paris Vendome hotel (we had chosen an 'extra special' hotel as it was our 5th Wedding Anniversary). We were not offered a refund for the cheaper night stay, nor were we offered a room upgrade when we returned the following day. The hotel did give us a bottle of champagne as an apology, and the staff were very apologetic, but we did feel that we had probably been bumped because we were not paying the full rate (we had got a very good deal with Eurostar) in place of a full paying customer.The Plaza Paris Vendome hotel is very stylish, set down a quiet street although there wasn't many restaurants near by to choose from. The Louvre is a 5 minute walk away, as is the nearest bus stop for the hop on/hop off bus which takes you to all the tourist attractions. The area is ideal if you love shopping at designer shops and boutiques as you are surrounded by them. Our room was quite small but there was plenty of room for the two of us. It was very nicely decorated and had a good sized bathroom (and the smallest bath I have been in!!!). We did find that the breakfast was expensive (29 Euros each for a very limited buffet), as was the bar - we had two irish coffees that came to 28 Euros!If you do decide to stay at this hotel it may be an idea to call them up a day or so before your stay to check they have a room for you so that you don't get any nasty suprises on arrival.

<Author>LondonFifi
<Content>Stylish hotel, good location. I stayed at the hotel in February 2005 for 3 nights. This is a fantastic hotel ?the best of many that I have used in Paris. I will definitely use it again. The hotel is very modern. The double room I had was quite small, but well designed. It had a great flat screen TV and the bed was incredibly comfortable. You can hire DVDs for your room from the front desk if you want to relax and watch something other than the news (English viewers).The bathroom was great with complementary Bulgari toiletries.There is a great swimming pool in the basement.I had breakfast at the restaurant attached to the hotel, it was average. The service wasn up to much and a bit of a disappointment considering how fabulous the rest of the hotel is. I think its better, and definitely cheaper, to eat out at a nearby caf. The hotel location is great. There are some lovely places to eat and there is a good food market nearby on a Saturday morning. Give this hotel a try and you won be disappointed.

<Author>LawyerAbroad
<Content>This is the best hotel I've stayed in in Paris This is a cracking hotel - we'd have no hesitation in going back.VALUE FOR MONEYWe spent a week at this hotel (2-9 Jan 2005) as part of a Eurostar package and it was superb and excellent value. Excluding the train cost, it worked out at 185 per night (roughly 260 Euro). We were given a complimentary upgrade to Deluxe room for the whole stay. If you haven't done so, its worth checking the Eurostar site - we tried to put together a package ourselvbes but didn't get near the price we paid through Eurostar.ROOM AND FACILITIES ETCThe hotel is still very new, and so is clean and modern. The room was pleasingly spacious, which is unusual in Paris. The only small gripe was no tea/coffee facility so it was mini bar, your own drinks or nothing. However, the room was generally excellent. The bathroom was also good size, modern and clean. The shower screen tended to leak , as someone else has observed, so hopefully they'll pick that up, but it was a minor worry. Good quality free toileries provided (Bulgari).The hotel has no view to speak of as it is on Rue de Mont Thabor, which is a small road one back from Rue de Rivoli (which runs down the side of the Tuileries). Some rooms face an interior enclosed space, so if you want a view of the street, ask for it. We realised that it was all too easy to see into some of the non-street facing rooms from the corridor accross the enclosed space, so if you want to be totally private, you should bear that in mind.STAFFThe staff were also superb. Rarely for France, all of them were polite and friendly, with the porters opening doors if you wafted near them, and the receptionists calling our good morning every day.FOODI can't comment on the food as we didnt eat in the hotel.LOCATIONThe location is perfect. The hotel is 2 minutes walk from Place Vendome, Place de la Concorde, and the Tuileries and the Louvre. This means its a bit further to the Eiffel tower and places like Sacre Coere, but frankly there's no way to be close to all of the sites and my view is being next to the Tuileries is the best you can do to cover most of them.Close by there are plenty of eateries, especially if you prefer a coffee and criossant locally instead of the hotel breakfast (which wasn't in our rate, and I think tends not to be in Paris rates - add an extra 26 Euros per person). Shops are also close by , though its perhaps 10 mins walk to the major department stores like Galleries LaFayette and Printemps. But you wont be short of shops if that's your thing.We were initially a bit concerned that there was an Irish pub on the corner of the road opposite the hotel, but there was no noise at all, and it was not a problem.You're also close to several Metro stations.TAXISWe had one bad expereince on the cost of a taxi booked via the hotel. The cost of our taxi from Gare du Nord to the Hotel was under 10 Euros. The return cost nearer 20 Euros, because the taxis clock seemed to run from being called up by the hotel. If you can bear it, try to grab one yoursleves!Have a great time !Michael in Manchester, England  
<Date>Jan 12, 2005

<Author>Contessa
<Content>A Romantic retreat-look out for the Valentines Day package! Charming and stylish this hotel should settle down to be one of Paris's finest.Staff were friendly and warm if a little overworked at times, our room was exquisite with every comfort and was extremely quiet.Breakfast was not a success on either morning, both the staffing levels and the food need more attention if staying here is to become a truly luxurious experience.The pool is attractive and a thoughtful addition for both leisure and business travellers alike. The Concierge service is excellent but with a 100% mark up on each ticket rather expensive and not something I'd met at other hotels. The limousine service is wonderful but frightfully overpriced-10 times the cost of a taxi to the Gare Du Nord for example!(It should cost you around 12 euros for 2 with luggage depending on traffic.)The public rooms are breathtaking, especially the reception area under it's glass pyramid but the library is so small it needs to become non smoking. We booked a package that was very good value, I suggest you do the same. The package didn't quite deliver on the hot chocolate and pastries but all in all we were pleased. I hope to go back in a year or two to see if the atmosphere has shaped up to that of Palazzo Sasso, my all time favourite. It is in the same group of hotels so I am optimistic that this can be achieved and I wish all the staff every success.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Superb French Luxury My husband took me to the Plaza as a birthday treat. What a hotel! As the saying goes...Small but perfectly formed. We felt welcome as soon as we entered the lobby, everything looks immaculate and the staff were interested and attentive. The location is great for museums, the theatre district and luxury shopping. The in-house restaurant called Pinxo was also very good (if it's fully booked you can eat at the counter and watch the chefs hard at work). Watch out for breakfast as if it's not part of a package it can be expensive (we paid 40 for scrambled eggs, an omelette, tea and toast), however that wouldn't stop us visiting again. Everything was as you'd expect in a hotel of this quality - from the rooms to the spa. This is a wholehearted recommendation and my only disappointment is that it's popularity will surely mean the prices will increase. Great hotel - well done!

<Author>kgs
<Content>Delightful for the most part We had a very nice experience at the hotel. Terrific concierge (Emmanuelle) who did a great job for us with tough to get local restaurant reservations. The staff at check in were also very nice. Rooms were lovely but very small. I don't understand how the owners expect people to unpack as we had to upgrade to a larger room to have enough room to be comfortable. Then, we were moved to a bigger room after a day because the internet connection was bad in our room after 24 hours of trying to get it fixed. Terrific room service quality--fruits, teas, breakfast was a treat. The pool and work out rooms were wonderful and the sauna and steam are co-ed so you can sweat with your partner! The restaurant in the hotel (kind of) was good and a welcome retreat for our first dinner. Location is really great, although the cab drivers have a hard time understanding our pronounciation of the street and name of the hotel and several times tried to take us to another hotel. Will recommend and return to the Plaza Paris Vendome Hotel for our next trip.

<Content>The Best Hotel In Paris! We stayed at the Plaza Paris Vendome from 2/11/04 to 4/11/04 and I can say it's the best hotel I've ever stayed in. We stayed at the prestigious Waldorf Astoria in New York last year, but the Plaza Paris Vendome is by far the better hotel.The rooms are a good size, superbly decorated, and include a flat screen TV and DVD. The bathroom is exceptional.One our last day I used the swimming pool and steam room. What a fantastic way to wake up! As it was off-season, I had the freedom of the facilities to myself.We didn't use the restaurant or the bar, as we usually like to find somewhere different each day. But by judging the overall standards of the hotel, I would suspect the restaurant is equally superb. I did order room service for breakfast, and again this was fantastic and not too expensive by Paris standards.I wouldn't stay anywhere else in Paris and definitely intend to go back soon!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Everything I Expected The other reviews here are accurate. We cross referenced expedia hotels with this web site and decided on this hotel on that basis. Spent our honeymoon there for 7 nights and was not disappointed.The only oddity was that the glass shower stall door did not seal properly. There was a visible gap between the hinge side of the door and the ceramic tile of the wall it was attached to. The first time I used the shower there was water all over the ceramic tile of the bathroom floor. All I had to do was ensure that the hand shower was pointing away from the door. The alternative was the use the beautiful, deep bath tub that was also available.I would go back again as long as the prices do not rise significantly. With all of the positive reviews available here the hotel may indeed raise them.Through expedia, after deducting air fare from the package we paid 271 euros per night for their basic room. In short it was relative value for the money by Paris standards.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Look no further - this place is brilliant What a fantastic hotel. I surprised my wife with this hotel for our anniversary.The place was ideally located near to the Tuileries Gardens, Place Vendome and the Louvre situated in a quiet back street. It is also very close to the Metro (Tuileries). The staff were all excellent. The porter brought up our luggage and we had no small notes with which to tip him. We saw him in the street later and he was more than happy to show us the way and so very helpful! After contacting the hotel before we came with regard to it being a special occasion - we were upgraded to a MASSIVE room and only paid the discounted rate of EUR 280. This being Paris, having a large room was a real luxury. We were on a corner with four double floor to ceiling windows - Plasma tv and DVD too. The beds were incredibly comfy, sheets and pillows of the highest standard.Bvlgari toiletries too! Drapes and blinds made the room totally dark and window soundproofing was very good. We didnt use the spa or pool but we really should have. It was so perfect we can't recommend this hotel enough. Everything in Paris is far closer together than you realise so getting anywhere is so easy and this hotel will definitely be our base when we return.Thank you especially to Severine!

<Author>SeattleMan
<Content>Lovely right bank refuge This is a small, personal luxury hotel two blocks from the Tuileries. We found a reduced rate on travelocity ($335/night = 280 euros) that was substantially less than published rates.The room was typically small, but the quality of everything, from the bed to the cabinets, draperies, sound-proofing, and bathroom, was excellent. Our only complaint is that the bathroom has a translucent door that allows day- or street-light into the sleeping area 24/7. The light is very diffuse and low level, but a surprising feature right next to heavy, opaque bedroom draperies. This can be a problem when jet lag wakens you at 3am.Staff were responsive and very pleasant, happy to speak a range of languages. We did not eat in the hotel restaurant or use the room service. The room fridge allows you to keep your own perishables in the room.The hotel has a lap pool - about 4 feet deep and 30 feet long- as well as a wonderful steam room and a sauna that provided a wonderful finish for long days of walking--or, more often, a refreshing break between the long day and a late Parisian dinner. I think I will stay on the left bank next time, where the strolling is less commercial and the pedestrians more local. But for the location and quality of accomodation Plaza Paris Vendme would be very hard to beat.
